Last updated: 13 March 2023

Editors’ citations

The list of sources given here provides publication details of items cited by the editors in their notes to letters and in other apparatus files. Citations to items in notes to letters not yet available on-line may be included: citations are added to the list when first added to the notes during all editing stages. As additional letters are edited and mounted on-line, this list will be updated.

Some titles were published in fascicles, the first of which may have been issued before the date on the title page. In this listing, the dates on title pages are preferred, as this is how they are catalogued in most general, and in some specialist, libraries. Where it is important to understand the date of actual publication in interpreting a letter in the Correspondence, known dates of publication of the relevant fascicle(s) or journal parts are given in the notes to that letter, often using the data in TL2. Thus the date of publication of the work given in this list should not be interpreted as the date of publication of any botanical name therein.

The transliteration of Cyrillic names is given as spelling used for the author in the source being cited, with cross references to the spelling most frequently used in the botanical literature, usually that which is given in the International Plant Name Index as the expansion of the ‘standard form’ used to indicate authorship of names. Some authors published under more than one transliteration, for example, Turczaninow, Turczaninoff, Tourczanow, the details of all of which are listed here under Turczaninow, to which the cross references lead. In the notes to the letters, citations are given to the transliteration used, also mentioning the transliteration under which the details will be found, such as ‘Turczaninoff [Turczaninow] (1863)’.

Places of publication are given using English names, for example, Vindobona is given as Vienna.

Where available, links are provided to the URL of a copy of those items that have been digitised. Preference has been given to sites using persistent links, such as doi, permalink, or handle URLs, and to links not behind a paywall, although if access is not available elsewhere links to sites commonly available through institutional or personal subscription are provided, for example to JSTOR and ProQuest. Links to the HathiTrust Digital Library are provided only if at the time of linking the item is available without geographical restriction. In a small number of cases, links have been provided to publicly available versions placed by authors in depositories; such links are provided on the understanding that authors have deposited items within the copyright or contractual arrangements they have with their publishers. If evidence of inappropriate deposit is found, these links will be removed.

For multi-volume works persistent links to a web-page with internal links to all volumes is preferred, otherwise the URL of the first volume of the set is given from which it is usually possible to find other volumes on the same site. In those cases where all volumes are not available on the same site, links are given to the volume cited in the notes to the letters. For items in journals or edited works preferred links are to the page where the text cited starts; where this is not possible a link to the whole item is used, and navigation tools on the site can be used to find the start of the article or chapter. Similarly, the only available links to newspapers are often to the relevant page, rather than directly to the item being cited.

There are some apparent idiosyncrasies in the sequence of items by an author within a year, for example Tate (1882) was published in December 1882, whereas Tate (1882a) and Tate (1882b) were published in January 1882, in the preceding volume of the journal. The sequence is a result of progressive editing of batches of the letters, and the addition of new citations in the order in which they were found.

Neither the Mueller Correspondence Project nor the Royal Botanic Gardens Victoria is responsible for the stability or persistence of the links provided.
